This is an enigmatic presence that both torments and seduces him, changin</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_78200022">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78200022" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1344527-dan-porter" class="left imgcol" title="Dan Porter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452409331p2/1344527.jpg" alt="Dan Porter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/78200022?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1344527-dan-porter" class="user" title="Dan Porter">Dan Porter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78200022">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6739976680636000097">The feeling I came away from <em>The Tooth Fairy</em> with was neither of happiness nor of satisfaction and, although it was a fairly dark story, neither was the feeling anything like despair. Somewhere between those points is some combination of recognition, rememberance, anticipation, and a sense of loss that make up the un-nameable feeling with which I connected with this book. This is a fairy tale and a coming of age story that combine beautifully to remind us of how much we lose and how much we gain</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6739976680636000097">The feeling I came away from <em>The Tooth Fairy</em> with was neither of happiness nor of satisfaction and, although it was a fairly dark story, neither was the feeling anything like despair. Somewhere between those points is some combination of recognition, rememberance, anticipation, and a sense of loss that make up the un-nameable feeling with which I connected with this book. This is a fairy tale and a coming of age story that combine beautifully to remind us of how much we lose and how much we gain as we grow up and to cause us to wonder if the losses and gains ever truly balance out. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6739976680636000097">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_115559971">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115559971" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2917516-janette-fleming" class="left imgcol" title="Janette Fleming"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1385651128p2/2917516.jpg" alt="Janette Fleming" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/115559971?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2917516-janette-fleming" class="user" title="Janette Fleming">Janette Fleming</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6439303-the-tooth-fairy" title="ebook 9780575082632" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer115559971">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11934749736385809040">Graham Joyce surely is one of the most underrated authors...is this possibly because he is so hard to market? Is he horror? Is he fantasy? Or possibly `social surrealism'...? <br /><br />What ever he is his stories are strange, magical and original and he fast becoming one of my favourite authors.<br /><br />He likes to instill in the reader a feeling of lingering uneasiness …. ‘You come away from the book feeling your perception of the world has been just been knock slightly askew away from what you previously thought</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11934749736385809040">Graham Joyce surely is one of the most underrated authors...is this possibly because he is so hard to market? Is he horror? Is he fantasy? Or possibly `social surrealism'...? <br /><br />What ever he is his stories are strange, magical and original and he fast becoming one of my favourite authors.<br /><br />He likes to instill in the reader a feeling of lingering uneasiness …. ‘You come away from the book feeling your perception of the world has been just been knock slightly askew away from what you previously thought to be normal’ Graham refuses to come down on one side or the other of the ideas he presents in his novel, it is all about ambiguity and uncertainty<br /><br />Sam, Clive and Terry are ordinary (ish) boys growing up in the 1960s until one day when Clive punches Sam in the mouth and knocks out a tooth. …Sam puts the tooth under his pillow at bedtime…as you do<br /><br />He wakes up during the night and first lays eyes on the Tooth Fairy “oddly dressed and smelling of horse’s sweat and chamomile”.<br /><br />Tinkerbelle this Fairy is not …it is an angry, bitter and viscous looking creature from nightmare.<br /><br />Thus begins a strange, disturbing sometimes touching relationship with the Tooth Fairy as it dogs Sam’s footsteps through childhood and into adolescence.<br /><br />The Tooth Fairy, whose appearance, mood and sex change constantly makes for a rather unpredictable, mercurial companion - sometimes protecting Sam other times tormenting him, bullying and threatening him and his family. The Fairy is a character in its own right with its own moods and emotions, jealously, lust, spite, anger and touching moments of tenderness. The author skilfully coveys the wild, unpredictable primeval nature of the Tooth Fairy.<br /><br />Without the supernatural element, the adolescent adventures of Sam and his friends would have made a brilliantly funny ‘rites of passage’ novel…all petty vandalism (though making pipe bombs in your Dad’s shed is hardly petty), growing pains and awakening sexuality.<br /><br />The novel is brilliantly structured, well characterised and entirely compelling and the elegant writing at times is almost prose with a whimsical and nostalgic tone.<br /><br />This novel shows that horror fiction doesn’t not have to be high octane ‘gore splatter’ serial killing zombies but that it can be beautiful, compulsive, hilarious, tragic, magical and very, very funny …oh very, very rude!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11934749736385809040">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1398541040">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398541040" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3639005-candi" class="left imgcol" title="Candi"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409332672p2/3639005.jpg" alt="Candi" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1398541040?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3639005-candi" class="user" title="Candi">Candi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=horror-creepy" class="actionLinkLite">horror-creepy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1398541040">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9304522800548153808"><em>"Through a window a broken fingernail of moon was visible. It barely illumined the intruder's face, but what Sam could see he didn't like. Two dark eyes, shiny like the green-black carapace of a beetle, flashed at him. The eyes were set deep, each in a squint counterpoised to the other, lurking under a matted shock of black hair. Tangled elf-locks framed high cheek bones and a swarthy complexion... A row of teeth glimmered in the faint moonbeams, a mouthful of blue light. The teeth were perfect,</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9304522800548153808"><em>"Through a window a broken fingernail of moon was visible. It barely illumined the intruder's face, but what Sam could see he didn't like. Two dark eyes, shiny like the green-black carapace of a beetle, flashed at him. The eyes were set deep, each in a squint counterpoised to the other, lurking under a matted shock of black hair. Tangled elf-locks framed high cheek bones and a swarthy complexion... A row of teeth glimmered in the faint moonbeams, a mouthful of blue light. The teeth were perfect, but, unless he was mistaken, they were sharpened to fine dagger points."</em><br /><br />Such a hideous, chilling and unconventional description of a favorite childhood fantasy figure seemed like a great start to this very bizarre novel. In the mood for a wicked scare during one of my favorite months of the year, I thought this book was just the ticket. Unfortunately, rather than peeking around corners and jumping at the slightest creak of the house or howl of the wind, I instead felt slightly revolted. Seven-year-old Sam looses a tooth and is surprised by a visit from this androgynous being. Sam will learn that this will be a recurring event throughout his childhood and adolescent years. This noxious and vulgar creature exhibits erratic moods, uses coarse language, changes from male to female and back again, and exploits the angst of a developing young man. All this seems to revolve around Sam's personal experiences, sexual awakenings and frustrations. As the tooth fairy points out to Sam, <em>"This is not a one-way thing, you know. You may think I'm your nightmare, but you in turn are my nightmare. It's your moods that pull me here."</em> The question becomes – is this being real or a manifestation of Sam's imagination during these critical coming-of-age years? An interesting concept, but when put into words and descriptions, it went way over the top for me. It became repetitive and unnerving rather than satisfyingly frightful.<br /><br />Despite my criticisms, I did find some really good points to this novel. For one, the characters are fairly well developed and memorable. Clive, Terry, Alice and Linda all suffer, along with Sam, from typical teenage concerns, get mixed up in various scrapes – some less innocent than others, and band together for support and camaraderie. Skelton, Sam's psychiatrist throughout this ordeal, is an interesting character with his own "demon", an addiction to alcohol. He may actually be the one to grasp some understanding of Sam's turmoil and the real reason for the presence of the tooth fairy in Sam's life. Also, when not foul, the writing was actually quite exceptional. I think Graham Joyce has a gift of vivid prose that has the potential to be quite gratifying: <em>"The earth under the snow was moist and brown, rich and curranty like a cake beneath a layer of marzipan. Breaking through the outlying trees, he found the woods made anew. Nothing stirred, and all noise from beyond the woods was baffled by the density of snow on the trees. The woods were stunned. It was a moment in closed time, a dream of ecstatic paralysis, a phase of Creation in which the trees waited impatiently to take on color, sound, texture."</em> This passage and others like it are the reason why I will most definitely give this author another try. 2.5 stars go to <strong>The Tooth Fairy</strong>, simply because overall I found it unsettling and somewhat unresolved in my mind by the end of the book.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9304522800548153808">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_111476614">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111476614" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="left imgcol" title="Mike (the Paladin)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450193915p2/2187043.jpg" alt="Mike (the Paladin)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/111476614?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="user" title="Mike (the Paladin)">Mike (the Paladin)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2293673.The_Tooth_Fairy" title="Hardcover 9780312862619" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer111476614">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9217924551819126344">Originally reviewed Jul. 2010<br />Updated July 2013<br /><br /><br />Some will like this book. I'm not one of them. While it has what I suppose strives to be a "touching ending" it can't change the rest of the book. This is one of a series of books (by that I don't mean a "series by the same author" I mean a series of books by various authors that treads similar ground) that have followed the same track over the last several years. It's not a new idea, it's the idea of taking an "established" literary form and "flippi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9217924551819126344">Originally reviewed Jul. 2010<br />Updated July 2013<br /><br /><br />Some will like this book. I'm not one of them. While it has what I suppose strives to be a "touching ending" it can't change the rest of the book. This is one of a series of books (by that I don't mean a "series by the same author" I mean a series of books by various authors that treads similar ground) that have followed the same track over the last several years. It's not a new idea, it's the idea of taking an "established" literary form and "flipping it". I've seen some "switched out" fairy tales that work very well and make good reads, I've also seen books that simply take old stories or folklore and instead of the "established lesson" usually taught in them we learn the way to live is to be a selfish, pushy, wisea**.<br /><br />This takes the tooth fairy "myth" (a story that could be used to scare children anyway...a being the sneaks in and out of your bedroom without your knowledge) and tells a fairly sinister and definitely adult tale. I won't try to lay out the story or give the ending revelation, no spoilers, but there are places here where the book veers very close to pedophilia, gives us several scenes of "boys/young men" discovering the joys of "self pleasuring", dances around what I suppose we'd call "childhood violence"... Don't be fooled by the title and let a "juvenile reader" near this one.<br /><br />Personally I find that the glow is off the idea of taking childhood stories and making them into R to NC17 rated fiction. Worse I didn't find the story itself involving enough to make these scenes a part of the telling. From Terry Pratchett and his tooth fairy with pliers to a short story I read some years ago about a tooth fairy who carved teeth out of mouths to use in magic, this is not truly an original idea and not a standout in story telling. <br /><br />I know many of you enjoyed it greatly, and for you I'm happy. But as I've said about other books, not for me. I brought the rating up to 2 stars as I've read far worse and don't want to rate the book down with the truly terrible reads I've run across...I wish we had a slightly "wider" rating system, maybe half stars. So, *1.5 stars* here. Just be aware what it is when you pick it up and if you think it will be your cup of tea, then fine. If you aren't interested in what is essentially a "lets rip the innocence away from another childhood myth novel"... well you're now forewarned. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9217924551819126344">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_39432661">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39432661" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1777325-julia" class="left imgcol" title="Julia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1413646019p2/1777325.jpg" alt="Julia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39432661?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1777325-julia" class="user" title="Julia">Julia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who aren't afraid of the dark</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1777325-julia?shelf=magical-realism" class="actionLinkLite">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39432661">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10150050105487702610">What I remembered, rather than learned, was how really terrifying childhood and adolescence can be! The character of the "Tooth Fairy", at once both horrifying and mesmerizing, wraps up all those childhood (pre-puberty) and teenage (puberty) fears into one repelling yet intriguing character. The story centers on 3 boys--Sam, Clive, and Terry--and begins with a large pike from the local pond biting off two of Terry's toes. It's a rollercoaster ride after that, and a dark one at that--imagine ridi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10150050105487702610">What I remembered, rather than learned, was how really terrifying childhood and adolescence can be! The character of the "Tooth Fairy", at once both horrifying and mesmerizing, wraps up all those childhood (pre-puberty) and teenage (puberty) fears into one repelling yet intriguing character. The story centers on 3 boys--Sam, Clive, and Terry--and begins with a large pike from the local pond biting off two of Terry's toes. It's a rollercoaster ride after that, and a dark one at that--imagine riding a rollercoaster alone in the dark by yourself, and that's how my stomach felt by the end. I can't imagine what fills Joyce's brain (spiders and centipedes, to say the least)--but he really wants to save these children from dark fears and knows he can't. So there's a desperation throughout the book--a long, dark road from Sam losing his first tooth to the boys/young men headed off to college. Linda and Alice serve mainly as foils, especially for the boys' sexual awakening, but Joyce managed to make me care for them as well. As usual, Joyce rips the comfortable veil off of reality, and what lies behind it, in this book, are the sharp, filed teeth of the Tooth Fairy. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10150050105487702610">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_739173279">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739173279" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/207385-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1301478135p2/207385.jpg" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/739173279?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/207385-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/207385-sarah?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/207385-sarah?shelf=group-read" class="actionLinkLite">group-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer739173279">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14026662210936071333">I have read several of Graham Joyce books and have thoroughly enjoyed them (<a title="Dark Sister by Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176334.Dark_Sister">Dark Sister</a> and <a title="The Limits of Enchantment by Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/160964.The_Limits_of_Enchantment">The Limits of Enchantment</a>) and I have wanted to read this one for a while. The Tooth Fairy is a book which is recommended by Stephen King and it was chosen as a group read in the Recommended by Stephen King Goodreads Group.<br /><br />So we've all heard of the tooth fairy and as a kid I remember putting my tooth under my pillow before bed and waking up the next morning with a quid (from my parents). This it exactly w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14026662210936071333">I have read several of Graham Joyce books and have thoroughly enjoyed them (<a title="Dark Sister by Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176334.Dark_Sister">Dark Sister</a> and <a title="The Limits of Enchantment by Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/160964.The_Limits_of_Enchantment">The Limits of Enchantment</a>) and I have wanted to read this one for a while. The Tooth Fairy is a book which is recommended by Stephen King and it was chosen as a group read in the Recommended by Stephen King Goodreads Group.<br /><br />So we've all heard of the tooth fairy and as a kid I remember putting my tooth under my pillow before bed and waking up the next morning with a quid (from my parents). This it exactly what Sam, a 7 year old boy, does when his tooth is knocked out when his friend punches him in the mouth. He doesn't tell his parents he's lost a tooth to see whether he still gets a pound and therefore proving the tooth fairy is real. Then while asleep, he is woken by somebody in his room and he sees none other than the tooth fairy himself. Or should I say herself. Or maybe itself as it seems to morph between male and female throughout the book which makes things really confusing in the story at times! And after the tooth fairy shows up loads of bad things happen and it all goes down hill for Sam and his friends.<br /><br />I didn't find the book scary but there is a definite feeling of unease which started early on in the book and built from there on in. The Tooth Fairy character itself was quite disturbing in its appearance and behaviours and extremely perverse. When it first shows up, the kid is about 7 - if it were me I think I'd have s**t my pants seeing it!<br /><br />I'm feeling pretty satisfied that I have all my adult teeth and not expecting (**touches wood**) to loose any teeth right now so I don't get a visit from the tooth fairy! S/He gives me the creeps.<br /><br />This is a very dark and disturbing tale. After reading the first third of the book, I had to stop for a while and read something lighter for a bit. And generally I don't have a problem with reading books which are on the darker side of life! If it hadn't been a group read, I think I may have abandoned the book completely but I persevered. I'm pleased I did as I did like the book; Joyce did a very good job at creating an atmosphere and building likeable characters, even if they were a bit messed up and did crazy things.<br /><br />It's the first coming-of-age book that I have read from a male perspective. And as a female, I found this both eye opening, interesting and shocking!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14026662210936071333">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_610383066">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610383066" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17499211-mike-carey" class="left imgcol" title="Mike Carey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442439396p2/17499211.jpg" alt="Mike Carey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/610383066?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 08, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17499211-mike-carey" class="user" title="Mike Carey">Mike Carey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer610383066">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer112901347341156060">I met Graham Joyce at Fantasycon last year and asked him which of his books would be the best one to start with. He recommended The Tooth Fairy, so I went ahead and picked it up. I went in blind, as it were - I didn't even read the blurb on the back of the book, and consequently had no idea what to expect.<br /><br />It was a very compelling read. There's a sense in which the storytelling is deliberately unstructured, depriving you of the usual clues to the direction the narrative is taking. This has the ef</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText112901347341156060">I met Graham Joyce at Fantasycon last year and asked him which of his books would be the best one to start with. He recommended The Tooth Fairy, so I went ahead and picked it up. I went in blind, as it were - I didn't even read the blurb on the back of the book, and consequently had no idea what to expect.<br /><br />It was a very compelling read. There's a sense in which the storytelling is deliberately unstructured, depriving you of the usual clues to the direction the narrative is taking. This has the effect of sharpening the horror, making you feel that everything is at stake, all the time. <br /><br />The tooth fairy itself is a unique creation - so much so that although the book stands in a well established tradition of "coming of age with supernatural stuff going on" stories, it really doesn't feel like anything I've read before. And the denouement, when it came, left me both breathless and profoundly moved. I'd imagined a lot of ways in which the narrator and his nemesis might finally settle what was between them, but I never came close to guessing what would happen.<br /><br />I confess I have a bias towards what I think of as generous horror - horror that allows you to empathise with the characters and makes you care what happens to them. The opposite, in fact, of sacrificial horror - where the characters exist primarily to be put through a wood chipper. The Tooth Fairy satisfies on an emotional level, and is still very, very scary.<br /><br />I'm going to read some more Graham Joyce, and soon.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="112901347341156060">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10698684920069036250">Graham Joyce blows me away. He writes sensually? That sounds a bit rude. He IS a bit rude. Earthy. You can almost feel and taste and smell, especially the leaf mold, and the musty smell of an old shed years after the suicide of its occupant.<br /><br />Here he writes about the evolution of a group of young boys, through to their departure for university. He manages to get right inside their (rather strange) world. The protagonist is (literally?) a character in the Tooth Fairy's nightmare.<br /><br />And when you think</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10698684920069036250">Graham Joyce blows me away. He writes sensually? That sounds a bit rude. He IS a bit rude. Earthy. You can almost feel and taste and smell, especially the leaf mold, and the musty smell of an old shed years after the suicide of its occupant.<br /><br />Here he writes about the evolution of a group of young boys, through to their departure for university. He manages to get right inside their (rather strange) world. The protagonist is (literally?) a character in the Tooth Fairy's nightmare.<br /><br />And when you think about the primeval nature and occasional near death experiences and close shaves of a little boy's life, know that Graham Joyce captures it.<br /><br />He may really be writing for a particular age group, but if you are still, or ever have, breathed, I suspect that you'd find this book easy to consume.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/6176678-lynne-cantwell" class="user" title="Lynne Cantwell">Lynne Cantwell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6176678-lynne-cantwell?shelf=psychological-horror" class="actionLinkLite">psychological-horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer205858973">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11198050292907522866">IMHO, Graham Joyce doesn't get enough respect in the US, despite the fact that he's won both the British Fantasy Award and the World Fantasy Award. Part of the problem may be that his work is hard to categorize, apart from putting it in the catch-all "speculative fiction" bin. <em>The Tooth Fairy</em>, for example, is psychological horror, maybe. Or maybe it's fantasy. It kind of depends on how you view what the main character is going through.<br /><br />Well, it's puberty that Sam is going through. But he's accomp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11198050292907522866">IMHO, Graham Joyce doesn't get enough respect in the US, despite the fact that he's won both the British Fantasy Award and the World Fantasy Award. Part of the problem may be that his work is hard to categorize, apart from putting it in the catch-all "speculative fiction" bin. <em>The Tooth Fairy</em>, for example, is psychological horror, maybe. Or maybe it's fantasy. It kind of depends on how you view what the main character is going through.<br /><br />Well, it's puberty that Sam is going through. But he's accompanied by a weird little creature that calls itself the Tooth Fairy. It shows only when Sam is alone, and it talks to him about the emotional ups and downs he's going through. A large part of what it says is disturbing -- disturbing enough that eventually Sam's parents take him to see a psychologist. So is Sam really crazy, or just a little crazy? Or is he really being visited by a creature from the dark side?<br /><br />I won't spoil it for you. But I will say that this book scared the pants off me, and made me a Graham Joyce fan.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11198050292907522866">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/645003-peejay-who-once-was-minsma" class="user" title="Peejay Who Once Was Minsma">Peejay Who Once Was Minsma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/645003-peejay-who-once-was-minsma?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42613580">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14480659491803649695">A brilliant evocation of coming-of-age in the sixties, juxtaposed with an hallucinatory sense of wonder--and terror. <br /><br />Sam, seven at the beginning of the story, has the misfortune of actually catching the tooth fairy in the act of switching tooth for cash. He/she becomes obsessed with Sam, dogging him through his adolescence. Alternately terrifying and erotic, loving and malevolent, male and female, this creature becomes Sam's constant secret and the fantastical backbeat of his life. <br /><br />In contrast t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14480659491803649695">A brilliant evocation of coming-of-age in the sixties, juxtaposed with an hallucinatory sense of wonder--and terror. <br /><br />Sam, seven at the beginning of the story, has the misfortune of actually catching the tooth fairy in the act of switching tooth for cash. He/she becomes obsessed with Sam, dogging him through his adolescence. Alternately terrifying and erotic, loving and malevolent, male and female, this creature becomes Sam's constant secret and the fantastical backbeat of his life. <br /><br />In contrast to the inhuman creepiness of the tooth fairy, the story of Sam and his friends from childhood to late adolescence as they explore the hash of growing up and finding their way in the world is charming, bittersweet, and very human. It's a tough balancing act to pull off, but Joyce manages it beautifully. This is an amazing book and an amazing bundle of emotions, from tears to laughing out loud.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17244057292349276247">The Tooth Fairy is a very good coming of age tale with sprinkles of horror (and maybe a wee fantasy, as well.) Sam has a Tooth Fairy - A (dream?) that is leaking over into the real world and causing havoc for the Redstone Moodies. As events unfold, Sam must find a way to disconnect from the Tooth Fairy and stop the intrusion into our world before it destroys all that he loves.<br /><br />Not a fast moving tale, Graham does a very good job creating an unsettlingly dark atmosphere. While it never gets fully r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17244057292349276247">The Tooth Fairy is a very good coming of age tale with sprinkles of horror (and maybe a wee fantasy, as well.) Sam has a Tooth Fairy - A (dream?) that is leaking over into the real world and causing havoc for the Redstone Moodies. As events unfold, Sam must find a way to disconnect from the Tooth Fairy and stop the intrusion into our world before it destroys all that he loves.<br /><br />Not a fast moving tale, Graham does a very good job creating an unsettlingly dark atmosphere. While it never gets fully realized into out and out horror to the bones, I was still left with a deep feeling of tension and unease as the story progressed. Very well written with superbly drawn characters. 4+ Stars! Highly Recommended! <br /><br /><em>I have had this one on my tbr for a long time and finally got around to it. I actually finished it the evening that I found out Graham had succumbed to Lymphoma. He will be sorely missed. Great writers live on thru their work though and I look forward to reading some more from Graham.</em><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1398464746">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11477161190595097236">For my enjoyment, probably a 2 star. It was just ok. For the writing though...probably a 3 star. It was vulgar, yes, but the writing was still good IMO. I don't think I'll easily forget, Terry, Sam, Clive, Alice, Linda....and even though a nasty character, the Tooth Fairy. I do think this book will stay with me.<br />I started thinking how much better this story could have been with these characters....had they not been so "mature" for their ages, used such foul language and in the case of the tooth f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11477161190595097236">For my enjoyment, probably a 2 star. It was just ok. For the writing though...probably a 3 star. It was vulgar, yes, but the writing was still good IMO. I don't think I'll easily forget, Terry, Sam, Clive, Alice, Linda....and even though a nasty character, the Tooth Fairy. I do think this book will stay with me.<br />I started thinking how much better this story could have been with these characters....had they not been so "mature" for their ages, used such foul language and in the case of the tooth fairy, been written so vulgar and vile. I did find them interesting. Even if more humor had been thrown in, it all could have come together for a more readable and enjoyable book. I really think there could have been a better story here. This little band of childhood friends and their exploits...add the fact that they went through so much. It could have been enhanced with the character of the tooth fairy if he/she had not been portrayed in such a loathsome way. It was just not fun to read in this form. G. Joyce is still a favorite author of mine and I plan to read his entire body of work.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17292701055953479215">(No spoilers)<br />A bold foul mouthed scary story.<br /><br />This reading was for my book club at Goodreads and the topic was "scary/horror". And indeed it was. I was totally taken by surprise by this coming-of-age novel about Sam and his friends.<br /><br />Sam lives in a small town in England with his parents. He is a typical boy until he looses a tooth at the age of seven and by some horrible mistake he can see the toothfairy, who is an ugly scary monster that will only cause trouble and disaster in Sams life. He is sen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17292701055953479215">(No spoilers)<br />A bold foul mouthed scary story.<br /><br />This reading was for my book club at Goodreads and the topic was "scary/horror". And indeed it was. I was totally taken by surprise by this coming-of-age novel about Sam and his friends.<br /><br />Sam lives in a small town in England with his parents. He is a typical boy until he looses a tooth at the age of seven and by some horrible mistake he can see the toothfairy, who is an ugly scary monster that will only cause trouble and disaster in Sam´s life. He is sent to a drunken psychiatrist, who is on to something, but Sam is caught up with being caught up by this thing. This continues untill we say goodbye to Sam at 14-years-old and moving to London. (no spoilers)<br /><br />The 4 star review (3,5) is partly the surprise of the content - and also the foul mouthed tooth fairy who does things, that you would normally refrain from reading to children. So it´s about these three boys coming of age, but if I had a 12-year-old, this would NOT be the goodnight-and-sleep-tight reading aloud book.<br /><br />On the other hand, that was what kept me going (I really don´t care about snotty teenangers), I just couldn´t wait to turn the pages of this fast moving forward, scary and funny novel, which is something I rarely experience.<br /><br />This quote is after Sam´s friend Terry got 2 toes bitten of by a Pike! (hilarious)<br /><br />Sam followed behind her, understanding that Terry was only five and life had taken away two of his toes, presumably for ever. He hoped for better luck for himself.<br /><br />-and this bold quote from when they have become a little older!<br /><br />Around the time Clive had been scheduled to take his special exam, his face exploded in a distressing case of acne....Someone at his school had even told him that his acne was caused by exessive masturbation. Clive, however, had the good sense to consult Terry and Sam about this last matter, both of whom were acne-free and yet admitted openly and candidly that they had become chronic maturbators.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_79868273">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79868273" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2905339-bark-s-book-nonsense" class="left imgcol" title="Bark's Book Nonsense"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451921873p2/2905339.jpg" alt="Bark's Book Nonsense" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79868273?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2905339-bark-s-book-nonsense" class="user" title="Bark's Book Nonsense">Bark's Book Nonsense</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2905339-bark-s-book-nonsense?shelf=disturbing" class="actionLinkLite">disturbing</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2905339-bark-s-book-nonsense?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2905339-bark-s-book-nonsense?shelf=dark-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79868273">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer734614543666800339">I loved this odd book and found it very difficult to put down. It's a character driven coming of age story about three young boys growing up in apparent normalcy. But underneath the veneer of normalcy simmers unexpected moments of darkness and danger. As the boys deal with life's many pitfalls -- growing up too smart, too dumb, too mediocre -- lurking in the shadows is a vicious tooth fairy which only one of them (Sam) can see. This tooth fairy is not the sweet version of childhood dreams but a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText734614543666800339">I loved this odd book and found it very difficult to put down. It's a character driven coming of age story about three young boys growing up in apparent normalcy. But underneath the veneer of normalcy simmers unexpected moments of darkness and danger. As the boys deal with life's many pitfalls -- growing up too smart, too dumb, too mediocre -- lurking in the shadows is a vicious tooth fairy which only one of them (Sam) can see. This tooth fairy is not the sweet version of childhood dreams but a nightmarish razor toothed, potty mouthed,<br />mischievous apparition and it's not at all pleased that Sam can see it.<br /><br />As Sam grows, the tooth fairy continues to show up unexpectedly and begins to change its form, becoming a chilling sexual thing that teases<br />and taunts and awakens odd feelings in Sam. Despite his fear of the tooth fairy the two have a weird sort of connection.<br /><br />This was most definitely a book that was anything but the "same-old, same-old" and I never could figure out quite where it was going next which is what I enjoyed so much about the book. The blend of the ordinary and the "weird" was seamless. Sam was a well developed, realistic character and watching him mature and grow was fascinating and I'm still pondering over the question "was it all in his imagination?" I'd like to think it wasn't.<br /><br />Overall a very creepy, touching, and perfectly bizarre book. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="734614543666800339">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer954687562">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12229764739373148838">I wish I could give 4.95 stars. The blurbs on the back of the book state : "Brilliant and unclassifiable", "Sharp, freshly imagined" "Complex and funny". All do a very poor job telling us about this book. They make is sound mundane. There is nothing mundane about this. I love the way Graham Joyce blurs the lines between "reality" and "fantasy". I find myself asking what do I think is real...what IS fantasy? There were points in this book that were laugh out loud moments, it could not be helped.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12229764739373148838">I wish I could give 4.95 stars. The blurbs on the back of the book state : "Brilliant and unclassifiable", "Sharp, freshly imagined" "Complex and funny". All do a very poor job telling us about this book. They make is sound mundane. There is nothing mundane about this. I love the way Graham Joyce blurs the lines between "reality" and "fantasy". I find myself asking what do I think is real...what IS fantasy? There were points in this book that were laugh out loud moments, it could not be helped. There were moments of quiet horror..."Did I just read what I read?". But most of all for me, this is a story about friendship. True friendship with all its trials and tribulations. Gorgeous.<br /><br />I have decided to change this to a five star book. I think of this story often and if people ask me, this is the book I tell them to read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12229764739373148838">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/198932-brian" class="left imgcol" title="Brian"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1186690329p2/198932.jpg" alt="Brian" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4300154?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 10, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/198932-brian" class="user" title="Brian">Brian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4300154">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12411875643330751537">It's hard to classify this book. I suppose you'd call it a fantasy but if that suggests magic etc., then that's altogether wrong. It's about a boy who is haunted by a nightmarish and sexually predatory tooth fairy. It's never entirely clear whether or not the tooth fairy is real or imagined. Though often disturbing, the book is also very funny and even poignant in its painfully detailed evocation of adolescence and there are some remarkably original flashes in the writing. Uncomfortable but comp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12411875643330751537">It's hard to classify this book. I suppose you'd call it a fantasy but if that suggests magic etc., then that's altogether wrong. It's about a boy who is haunted by a nightmarish and sexually predatory tooth fairy. It's never entirely clear whether or not the tooth fairy is real or imagined. Though often disturbing, the book is also very funny and even poignant in its painfully detailed evocation of adolescence and there are some remarkably original flashes in the writing. Uncomfortable but compelling.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12411875643330751537">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/226335-tressa" class="left imgcol" title="Tressa "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1378092828p2/226335.jpg" alt="Tressa " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/54683844?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 14, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/226335-tressa" class="user" title="Tressa ">Tressa </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/226335-tressa?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer54683844">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11431900504430487483">I don't even know how to describe this book. It was not anything like I expected it to be. I guess I thought it would be an outright horror book about a being called the Tooth Fairy. But the story is a mixture of McCammon's Boy's Life and King's "The Body."<br /><br />I agree with another reviewer that not much really happens in the story. It's not a bad story, but it just kind of limped along to the ending.<br /><br />Can't say I'd recommend this book to anyone.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_59366440">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59366440" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2160536-marvin" class="left imgcol" title="Marvin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381556565p2/2160536.jpg" alt="Marvin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/59366440?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2160536-marvin" class="user" title="Marvin">Marvin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer59366440">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18219582221855078818">Three and a half stars. <em>The Tooth Fairy</em> isn't really a horror novel. I'm not entirely sure it is even supernatural. What I'm sure about is that this is the strangest coming-of-age novel I've ever read. On the night he loses a tooth, seven year old Sam places it under his pillow and in turn encounters a strange creature who is like no tooth fairy that you have ever heard of. The tooth fairy and Sam become connected through his childhood as the creature appears and reappears taunting and seducing</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18219582221855078818">Three and a half stars. <em>The Tooth Fairy</em> isn't really a horror novel. I'm not entirely sure it is even supernatural. What I'm sure about is that this is the strangest coming-of-age novel I've ever read. On the night he loses a tooth, seven year old Sam places it under his pillow and in turn encounters a strange creature who is like no tooth fairy that you have ever heard of. The tooth fairy and Sam become connected through his childhood as the creature appears and reappears taunting and seducing him. Sam and his group of friends aren't entirely normal themselves. They are essentially outsider kids getting into fairly serious trouble. Is this the work of the Tooth Fairy or simply disturbed children? It's not entirely clear. What is clear is that this is a story with Freudian <em>and</em> Jungian references that hooks the reader in with its quite heavy sexual overtones. Did I say overtones? Actually this book is sexually explicit to the extreme and not necessarily in a pleasant way. It is disturbing reading but rings with truth in its depiction of adolescent angst and sexual awakening. This is not a book that you can read and then forget about. I will be thinking about this novel and what it means for a long time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18219582221855078818">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer978705504">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer560765936565979061"><div>Yes, Jennifer, I enjoyed this book. Is <a title="Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Graham%20Joyce">Graham Joyce</a> the best thing since sliced bread? I'm not so sure.<div><br /></div> <div>This is a fascinating story about three boys, a slightly older girl, and a tooth fairy. But nothing really happens. We see the boys grow up and do all the things completely ordinary boys do. Sure Sam has sex with a tooth fairy, and Terry loses his toes to a pike, and there's a murder (well, one that they're directly involved in, plus the murder/suicide of the rest of Terry's family), but what</div></div></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText560765936565979061"><div>Yes, Jennifer, I enjoyed this book.  Is <a title="Graham Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Graham%20Joyce">Graham Joyce</a> the best thing since sliced bread? I'm not so sure. <div><br /></div>
<div>This is a fascinating story about three boys, a slightly older girl, and a tooth fairy. But nothing really happens. We see the boys grow up and do all the things completely ordinary boys do. Sure Sam has sex with a tooth fairy, and Terry loses his toes to a pike, and there's a murder (well, one that they're directly involved in, plus the murder/suicide of the rest of Terry's family), but what little action there is seems so merely incidental. And then the boys grow up. The end.</div>
<div><br /></div>
<div>And yet, it's still hauntingly beautiful. My wife was much less conflicted about it, and read it in an evening.</div>
</div></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1181982634">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181982634" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/28743856-rj" class="left imgcol" title="Rj"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1392751306p2/28743856.jpg" alt="Rj" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1181982634?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/28743856-rj" class="user" title="Rj">Rj</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1181982634">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15594429002355950669">On a recommendation from Powell's Review-a-day I picked up Graham Joyce's The Tooth Fairy. After picking up the book it was hard to put it back down, but I managed to stretch reading it over two nights, savouring Joyce's minimalist and sparse writing style. The book is a macabre, albeit nostalgic look back at a young boy's entrance into manhood and his twisted relationship with a tooth fairy that only he can see. Joyce's Tooth Fairy gestures to the fairies of old England, like the dark and magic</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15594429002355950669">On a recommendation from Powell's Review-a-day I picked up Graham Joyce's The Tooth Fairy. After picking up the book it was hard to put it back down, but I managed to stretch reading it over two nights, savouring Joyce's minimalist and sparse writing style. The book is a macabre, albeit nostalgic look back at a young boy's entrance into manhood and his twisted relationship with a tooth fairy that only he can see. Joyce's Tooth Fairy gestures to the fairies of old England, like the dark and magical characters out of The Brothers Grimm. These are not the the fairies of modern mythology, sanitized and Disneyized for childhood consumption. Joyce's fairy is like the sprites and magical creatures who are neither, good nor evil, but rather mischievous in spirit. They are like the woods they come from, wild by nature and unfettered by mortal boundaries and ideologies. The book manages to capture the diversity of feelings which collect in each of us as we pass through adolescence. Reading Joyce's work reminded me of Douglas Glover's book Elle. Both authors create magical worlds with words which seem to exist somewhere between our own and a mythological world we only sense in that time between dreaming and waking.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15594429002355950669">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18177815-sumit-singla?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1377235044">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9359127286645579192">What initially intrigued me about this book was that Stephen King (one of my favourite authors) had recommended it. However, a few hours after having finished this, I feel more than a bit let down.<br /><br />The books begins with the adventures of three friends - Sam, Clive and Terry with the somewhat macabre incident of Terry having two toes bitten off by a pike. <br /><br />Life goes topsy-turvy with the entrance of a hermaphroditic 'tooth fairy' - a malevolent creature with unstated ambitions, who stalks Sam and le</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9359127286645579192">What initially intrigued me about this book was that Stephen King (one of my favourite authors) had recommended it. However, a few hours after having finished this, I feel more than a bit let down.<br /><br />The books begins with the adventures of three friends - Sam, Clive and Terry with the somewhat macabre incident of Terry having two toes bitten off by a pike. <br /><br />Life goes topsy-turvy with the entrance of a hermaphroditic 'tooth fairy' - a malevolent creature with unstated ambitions, who stalks Sam and leads to one event after another.<br /><br />The story is filled with Freudian references and fair bits of sexual exploits. The premise is interesting enough, but the idea runs out of steam about mid-way. That's when you start seeing the fairy as an annoyance instead of a terrifying creature of magic.<br /><br />Much of the sex is oddly contrived and the 'human-magical creature' interaction becomes tedious to read beyond a point.<br /><br />I don't know Stephen King's reasons for recommending this, but I sure ain't following suit!<br /><br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/2907291-glenda" class="left imgcol" title="Glenda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1320940043p2/2907291.jpg" alt="Glenda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/969943643?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2907291-glenda" class="user" title="Glenda">Glenda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2907291-glenda?shelf=books-read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">books-read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer969943643">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8748835491275856186">Sam and his friends are like any normal gang of normal young boys--roaming wild around the outskirts of their car-factory town, daring adults to challenge their freedom; then one day Sam wakes to find the tooth fairy sitting on the edge of his bed--but this is not the sweet version of childhood dreams but a nightmarish razor toothed, potty mouthed, mischievous apparition and it's not at all pleased that Sam can see it. As Sam grows, the tooth fairy continues to show up unexpectedly and begins to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8748835491275856186">Sam and his friends are like any normal gang of normal young boys--roaming wild around the outskirts of their car-factory town, daring adults to challenge their freedom; then one day Sam wakes to find the tooth fairy sitting on the edge of his bed--but this is not the sweet version of childhood dreams but a nightmarish razor toothed, potty mouthed, mischievous apparition and it's not at all pleased that Sam can see it. As Sam grows, the tooth fairy continues to show up unexpectedly and begins to change its form, becoming a chilling presence that both torments and seduces him, changing his life forever. <br /><br />After reading several Graham Joyce novels, I was looking forward to reading his most popular--The Tooth Fairy. But after reading it, I'm a little disappointed. This story didn't seem to go anywhere, and I spent most of the book trying to decide whether the Tooth Fairy was real or just a figment of Sam's imagination. (I'm still not quite sure). Usually the supernatural elements are the best parts of a Joyce novel but this one just seemed weird. The Tooth Fairy was just too vulgar and disgusting for me to relate to. I read this with my book group and most were disappointed. Don't judge Graham Joyce by this novel. Read some of his others--which are much better IMO.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8748835491275856186">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1106010248">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106010248" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/77467-aaron" class="left imgcol" title="Aaron"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224367343p2/77467.jpg" alt="Aaron" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1106010248?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/77467-aaron" class="user" title="Aaron">Aaron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/77467-aaron?shelf=esoteric-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">esoteric-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1106010248">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17309974749653791167">Meandering and sometimes meanspirited, Joyce's novel is that rare beast of a coming-of-age story (I'd call it a bildungsroman but I'm not sure the main characters actually learned anything) that defies all conventionality, instead heads in a million disparate directions at once, and comes up bloody roses. The fantastic lives alongside the real, but in shadows, just out of view to everyone else besides one character, and the reader. The characters are children, but the situations presented are de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17309974749653791167">Meandering and sometimes meanspirited, Joyce's novel is that rare beast of a coming-of-age story (I'd call it a bildungsroman but I'm not sure the main characters actually learned anything) that defies all conventionality, instead heads in a million disparate directions at once, and comes up bloody roses. The fantastic lives alongside the real, but in shadows, just out of view to everyone else besides one character, and the reader. The characters are children, but the situations presented are decidedly adult, accurately casting an adolescent's fixation on sex as a central tenet of the story. I can't bring myself to describe the plot, but it's the gorgeous prose itself and the tone of the tale that works so many of the wonders here: wistful and wondrous in turns, there's a sense of deep melancholy mixed with palable paranoia, excitement and lust running headlong into fleeting bursts of horror. Tragedy underscores much of the action here, and we're left wondering why, though it's clear it's just the way of the world; perhaps the fantastical elements are simply a coping mechanism? Hard to say, and no matter. This is one of the best books I've read in ages, and exactly what I needed, when I needed it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17309974749653791167">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The dead baby\'s teenage mother and other passers-by swear the wind caused the carriage to roll, and the police take Josh for a troublemaker when he insists on writing a statement to the contrary. Shaken, Josh hits the road again, only to find that it\'s not so easy to get away from Furnace; something inhuman is hot on his heels. A pretty hitchhiker recognizes a mysterious scrap of writing in his truck as ancient runes spelling out--on human skin--a horrific curse. From then on, all roads lead back to Furnace as Josh races to unscramble a weird puzzle involving a wealthy town councilor, the Philosopher\'s Stone, and a demon who will destroy Josh in three days unless he returns the runes to their rightful place.  The rotating point of view can be confusing, and the language (Gray is Scottish) occasionally doesn\'t ring true to an American ear.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25027.Graham_Joyce">About Graham Joyce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/25027.Graham_Joyce"><img alt="25027" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1425749570p2/25027.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer15008029807148520251">Graham Joyce (22 October 1954 – 9 September 2014) was an English writer of speculative fiction and the recipient of numerous awards for both his novels and short stories. <br /><br />After receiving a B.Ed. from Bishop Lonsdale College in 1977 and a M.A. from the University of Leicester in 1980. Joyce worked as a youth officer for the National Association of Youth Clubs until 1988. He subsequently quit his po</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15008029807148520251">Graham Joyce (22 October 1954 – 9 September 2014) was an English writer of speculative fiction and the recipient of numerous awards for both his novels and short stories. <br /><br />After receiving a B.Ed. from Bishop Lonsdale College in 1977 and a M.A. from the University of Leicester in 1980. Joyce worked as a youth officer for the National Association of Youth Clubs until 1988. He subsequently quit his position and moved to the Greek islands of Lesbos and Crete to write his first novel, Dreamside. After selling Dreamside to Pan Books in 1991, Joyce moved back to England to pursue a career as a full-time writer.<br /><br />Graham Joyce resided in Leicester with his wife, Suzanne Johnsen, and their two children, Joseph and Ella. He taught Creative Writing to graduate students at Nottingham Trent University from 1996 until his death, and was made a Reader in Creative Writing.<br /><br />Joyce died on 9 September 2014. He had been diagnosed with lymphoma in 2013.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15008029807148520251">...more</a>
